Automotive Gleanings from Overseas 220

— Yu

Ford Exhibits 100 Types of Automobiles: Ford Motor Company recently exhibited over 100 types of automobiles produced over the years in Detroit. Everything from commercial to personal transportation is included. In brief, these include grocery trucks with awnings, refrigerator trains, coal delivery trucks, garbage trucks, furniture trucks, large buses for schools or public use, street sweepers, milk delivery trucks, oil tanker trucks, gasoline trucks, and various types of vehicles used in municipal or agricultural settings. The newly released Ford AA trucks are also on display. The wheelbases vary between 131.5 inches and 157 inches. The various cars of the AA model can also be fitted with different bodies for various uses.

(The recent global economic panic has reached its peak. This year's automobile industry operations will definitely suffer major losses, right?) A reporter from the Weekly Post deliberately asked with a determined tone.

An Ideal Automobile 221

— Tang Tiyun

Several years ago, a wealthy young man, Mr. A, visited the studio of a famous American car body designer and requested the creation of an ideal automobile.

Mr. A said: (I deeply understand the need for a car. But how to design this car, I am a layman. In short, on sunny days, I will lower the convertible top to make it a sports car and fully enjoy the natural scenery. But when necessary, the convertible top can transform it into a sedan. Normally, it only provides seating for two people, but occasionally, if there are two more people, it should not affect the comfort of each person. The appearance should be as rich as possible while also expressing an air of dignity. Whether on broad avenues, tree-lined roads, fast driving, or slow driving, each should be extremely suitable. This is my ideal automobile.) The designer pondered for a moment and smiled, saying: (I have also thought like this. Perhaps it can be realized in the future to meet your needs.)

Now, this ideal automobile has become a reality. It is the Studebaker Free-Wheeling President Eight-Cylinder Four-Season Roadster.

News

Tong-Yu Route Selected 222

— Shan Lang

The Tong-Yu Road is the main land transportation artery between Sichuan and Guizhou provinces. After repeated consultations between the two sides, the Sichuan authorities favored Wen-shui as the connecting point, and some people in Guizhou also agreed. However, the Wen-shui route is only slightly flat in Sichuan, while in Guizhou, large mountains span across it, making it unsuitable for use as a provincial road. The Guizhou authorities specifically ordered Dou Shanxiang, the director of the Tong-Yu Highway Survey Team, to personally visit the Sichuan authorities to discuss changing the connecting point and conducting a joint survey. This was approved, and the Chongqing Survey Team sent Chief Engineer Shen and others to Songkan to conduct a joint on-site survey. As a result, the Xin-Song route was adopted, with Chong-xi-gou as the Sichuan-Guizhou connecting point. Now, Mr. Dou has returned to the province after completing his mission and published a comparative description of the Xin-Song route selection reasons and the engineering of each route. Excerpts are as follows:

The Tong-Yu Avenue originally passed through Xin-Song. The mountains are high and the terrain is extremely dangerous. Anyone who has passed through knows that the road is impassable. Before the team conducted the survey, it was expected that this section of the road must bypass Wen-shui. Therefore, upon reaching Tongzi, the team split up and conducted on-site inspections. One route went from Tongzi via Jiuba, Zhangyangba, Wenshui, and Shihao to Ganshui. Another route went from Tongzi via Maotian, Chumipu, Luoyangxi, Liangfengya, Huabeiping, Tianshuichi, Shanpo, Xinzhan, Songkan, Jiudianya, and Guanyinqiao to Ganshui. Another route exited Luoxigou and went via Yejiba, YanYan, Xiaojiupan to Ganshui. Yet another route went out of Maliu, Yangcun, Anhe, Huaqiutang, and down to Xinzhan, then followed the river out of Songkan Fishing Cave to Ganshui. In addition, several comparative lines were surveyed near difficult sections such as Chaomipu, Dapo, and XiongHuangsi Bazhuaxi on the Xin-Song line. After several months of time, the results of the survey of each route showed that the old Xin-Song road was indeed difficult to build. However, there are good routes near the old road. Whether compared in terms of route length, slope, engineering, economics, or the prosperity of towns along the way, it is superior to other routes. After the Chongqing Survey Team conducted an on-site survey, they also changed their proposal to use Wen-shui as the connecting point and expressed their agreement. After the Xin-Song road was selected, some people were not surprised but suspicious, and some even raised objections. Now, I will compare the advantages and disadvantages of each surveyed route and explain the situation obtained to dispel the doubts of the general public.

(1) Xin-Song Route: This line starts from the edge of the North Gate of Tong City, passes through Maotian, Shuimotang, Sanzuosi, Chumipu, Luoyangxi, Liangfengya, Niugundang, Huaqiuping, Jiaoshan, Tianshuichi, Yingzuiyan, Tudiping, Dawoodang, Changziyan, Liujiashan, Tunyan, Damaopo, Shanpo, Xinzhan, Mengdu, Caoxieya, Jiulonggou, Banpo, Qinggangshao, Guankou, Qizhenxi, Chenghuangsi, Sangyuanba, Liangfengya, Qingshui Creek, Dabao Pu, Songkan Fenwan, Ma'anshan, Bazhuaxi, Guanyinyan, Hanjiaodian, Yantoushang, Baiyangping, Jiudianya, Damianpo, and reaches Chongxigou, connecting to the Sichuan border. The total length is 160 li. The route is straight. From Tong City to Chumipu, it is 20 li and completely flat. The earth and rock mountain is no more than ten feet high, and the bridges are only three or four small bridges a few feet wide. From Chumipu, it slopes up to Huaqiuping, and then slopes to reach Shanpo for more than 40 li. It can avoid the extremely large Yan Mountain of Zushi Guan Shi Niu Lan, and the slope is long and gentle. Sharp bends are also very rare. Furthermore, 80 to 90 percent of the area is pure soil. The rock mountain route is only about one-tenth. From Shanpo via Xinzhan to Mengdu, it is 20 li and the route is flat. There is less rock and more soil. The rock mountain section is only four or five li. The entire section is sandy, making it extremely easy to excavate. Furthermore, the existing Mengdu Bridge can be used, reducing tens of thousands of bridge construction costs. From Mengdu, it slopes up to Caoxieya, then passes smoothly along the hillside to reach Qinggangshao. Then, it descends slowly to Qizhenxi for 20 li. The dangers of the Jiulong Three Valleys are transformed into a flat, gentle slope. Moreover, most of it is mud, and the rock is sandy, making the work extremely easy. The section from Qizhenxi directly to Songkan is about 30 li and is also flat. There is even more farmland. The rock mountain sections are only at Chenghuangsi, Liangfengya, Qingshui Creek, and Waiyanzi, where each rock is no more than 40 feet long and is sandy, requiring little effort. From Songkan, it slopes up to Jiudianya, then descends to Chongxigou, which is 8 li. Although it is a sloping route, the slope is gentle, and sharp bends are also very rare. The soil mountain route accounts for about 80 percent. The rock mountain section is only at Ma'anshan, Bazhuaxi, Guanyinyan, and the top of Yantou, totaling no more than four or five li. Digging a zhang-wide rock and building a few-foot-high embankment roadbed can be quickly completed. This is the most significant project of the entire line. However, it will only cost tens of thousands of dollars, which is not much. In summary, the rock mountain route is only about one-tenth of the entire line, while the soil mountain route accounts for nine-tenths. The laborers find it easier to work, and success is naturally easier. More than ten li of rock mountains only require about 110,000 yuan. However, there are slightly more embankments, requiring about 130,000 yuan. As for bridges, there are only more than 40, requiring about 70,000 yuan. The total is only more than 300,000 yuan. Therefore, this line is not only straight and saves on construction costs for both provinces, but also has dense towns along the way, making it easier to develop than other lines. Even if the Sichuan border is temporarily impassable, we only need to repair to Songkan to connect with the waterway and obtain the convenience of water and land transportation. Compared to other lines, it has many advantages. Therefore, the Xin-Song line is indeed worth adopting.

(2) Comparison with the Wenshui Line: This line starts from Tongzi Guandu River, follows the Tong-Chi-Ma Road route, passes through Yangliuping, Jiuba, Zhangyangba, and reaches Wenshui. Then, it branches off from Wenshui and passes through Shihao to reach Ganshui. Most of the Tong-Wen section has been excavated. Only 30 li need to be newly built from Wenshui to connect to the Sichuan border. Before the survey, the Sichuan and Guizhou authorities and the surveyors on both sides expected that the Tong-Yu route would definitely pass through here. The Sichuan side even made a decision to use Wenshui as the border point. However, the survey results showed that this line is 120-130 li longer than the Xin-Song line, with each station being longer in Sichuan and Guizhou. Moreover, the route is poor. Although it is slightly flat in Sichuan, the Guizhou section, except for the section from Zhangyangba via Wenshui to the Sichuan border, is slightly flat, but the 100 li from Zhangyangba to Tongzi are all mountains and ridges spanning across it. The route has large undulations and many sharp bends. Furthermore, the slope is large, exceeding 10 percent in many places, making it unsuitable for use as a provincial road. It is not as straight as the Xin-Song line and has fewer curves. Even in terms of engineering, although more than half of the earthwork has been completed, there are still bare slopes that have not been worked on at all. Furthermore, after years of erosion by rainwater, it is feared that no more than half of the project has been completed. The old road of 200 li between Tong-Wen has human paths, but only two stations of the road, and the repair of the curves really have more than three stations. The new construction engineering of 30 li outside of Wenshui, totaling nearly the whole new construction engineering of Xin-Song's whole line, and the special engineering of the bridges, culverts, rock dikes, etc., has not even started. According to the estimate of the Chief of the Guichi Road Engineering, the Tongzi county's special engineering expenses will cost 290,000. Shuishui county's expenses will cost more than 700,000. According to this, the least amount it will cost from the Tongzi region to Wenshui will be 300,000. If one adds Wenshui to the Sichuan region, it will also take four or five thousand. The total special engineering expenses required will be about 600,000, which is double the 300,000 of the Xin-Song line. It is not known if it is worthwhile or not. Even if the Wen line is completed, vehicles are more expensive to transport. Neither time nor wealth is economical. The transport and local development along the way would not have any great prospects. The Guizhou-Yu Line not being here, but by Xin Song, has great reasons to exist. (To be continued.)

Marshal Foch's War Diary 224

— Translated by Gu Angruo

Therefore, if our army does not give the enemy enough time to reorganize their ranks, the enemy forces will surely be in a chaotic state, and our offensive can advance like a sharp knife cleaving bamboo.

The enemy's numerous machine guns firing simultaneously are indeed sufficient to slow down our covering retreat, but are not enough to constitute a strong defense.

Given the situation, our army often has to find ways to break through the enemy's lines. Our infantry and artillery units must designate targets sufficient to break the enemy's lines for the attack.

The following points are quite important:

(A) Corps should identify the most important distant targets.

(B) Divisional units should select intermediate targets.

(C) Regiment and battalion troops should launch accurate, swift, and fierce attacks on enemy machine gun nests that are hindering our advance.

The future development of the battle hinges on the efforts of the corps commander and division commanders, as well as the soldiers' lives.

On September 26th, after a fierce artillery bombardment, the U.S. First Army and the French Fourth Army followed suit at 5:30 a.m. and 5:25 a.m., respectively, and separately began the (B)(C) offensive. The entire attacking force immediately progressed between the Meuse River and the Suippe River, occupying the enemy's first line of defense, with an average advance of two to three miles.

In order to closely follow the development of the battle, I moved to the Villa Teleriafontaine on the afternoon of the 26th (north of Saint-Dizier). I also stayed there on the 27th. During the day, I visited Commander Pétain in Nadon Valley and also went to the headquarters of General Gérard Chrétien-Jean Lelong Saint-Maur.

On the 27th and 28th, the enemy resisted stubbornly. The French Fourth Army was stalemated on the German lines in the Py River basin. The U.S. First Army, after being suddenly attacked from the Argonne side, stopped around Apremont.

On September 29th, the French Fourth Army concentrated its forces in the middle and launched a fierce attack, breaking through the Py River line and driving the enemy back to the second line between the Chiers River, the Py River, and Montfaucon-d'Argonne. However, the U.S. Army was trapped between the Meuse River and the Argonne River, where the terrain was very narrow, and it was difficult to march due to the mountains and rivers. The enemy's flank attacks from the Argonne side and the east bank of the Meuse River were still insurmountable. The U.S. Army wanted to increase the strength of the first line to overcome these difficulties, but not only was it futile, but the coordination between the front and rear of the army was also ineffective, and all lines of communication were cut off.

In order to remedy the situation, I agreed with Commander Pétain and decided to withdraw several divisions from the U.S. front line, some to the east of the Meuse River, and some to the west of the Argonne River, and advocated incorporating them into the French corps on the front line to avoid wasting time. The French and American troops on both banks of the Meuse River were under the command of General Pershing, and another French general (Second Army) was appointed to command the Allied forces on both banks of the Argonne River. (To be continued)

The World of Cigarettes 225

— 16

Before 1492, no civilized country in the universe even dreamed of having such a thing as cigarettes. The originator of smoking can be said to be the Red Indian of America. They rolled tobacco leaves into long shapes and put them in pipes, and then smoked. Our current paper-rolled cigarettes are just a later variation.

There are many places in the world that produce tobacco leaves, such as Canada, India, Egypt, and Turkey. Our country also has tobacco leaves in Xuchang and Qingzhou. However, the place with the largest production and the best tobacco leaves in the world is in Virginia in the eastern United States.

The total number of cigarettes consumed worldwide is unknown because there has not been a detailed survey, so accurate reports are impossible to obtain. However, in the United States alone, 115,000,000,000 cigarettes are consumed each year, invisibly spending more than $1,500,000,000. It sells 1,000,000,000 cigarettes in its British Strait Settlements, 250,000,000 cigarettes in Burma, and 1,000,000,000 cigarettes in the Philippine Islands. As for China, even more are imported, totaling 38,500,000,000 cigarettes. In summary, the total number of cigarettes consumed in various parts of the world is not as much as in the Far East countries.

Medical News 227

▲Aishi Pharmacy claims that its secret family-made surgical medicine, Huanji Cream, specializes in treating all kinds of sores, damaged hands and feet, unnamed carbuncles, scabies, scalds, cuts, bruises, and carbuncles. When encountering the above symptoms, applying the cream will immediately stop the pain and itching, draw out toxins, reduce swelling, remove decay, and promote new tissue growth. It has always been praised by people from all walks of life. Recently, the weather has been hot, and sores are rampant, making the cream very popular. It is sold in Sincere, Wing On, Sun Sun, and major company pharmacies and shops.

▲Datongsheng Chinese Medicine Store, located at the southern end of Rue Chaleux in the French Concession, claims that it was established by wealthy merchant Xu Jianshan. After preparing for several months in a newly built three-story Western-style building, it recently opened. The first day's business reached as high as seven or eight thousand yuan, and has continued at around a thousand yuan per day. The store personally procures ginseng, bird's nest, and deer antlers, and carefully supervises the production of pills, powders, and decoctions, which customers are extremely satisfied with. The other night, the store held a banquet for guests and friends at the Doyichu Sichuan Restaurant. Despite the stormy weather, attendance was very enthusiastic. Lu Hanjun and others provided courteous hospitality, making it a grand occasion. During the banquet, famous doctors Yang Zhitian and Yin Yifu successively spoke, painfully recounting the decline of the national essence and the harm of the outflow of rights and interests, moving all those who listened. The guests and hosts dispersed happily until late at night. Furthermore, in view of the recent widespread flooding, the store, feeling heartbroken, initiated a proposal by Manager Xu Zheng to automatically donate one day's income within the next few days, along with its own donations, to relief organizations for distribution to the disaster areas, to do its part.
